I really like it here! The management team is awesome, super helpful with a move from overseas during covid. They communicate really well and schedule food truck visits and little things for the community (as much as they can with covid). The maintenance team works really hard to maintain the grounds and the units, I always see people picking up trash, gardening, etc. The apartments are nice and updated, pet friendly, high ceilings, washer/dryer, nice patio. The grounds are really nicely landscaped, its like a little oasis. Little dog park which is great, and people are always walking their dogs on the little loop around the apartment complex, so I've actually met a few neighbors.I've had a couple things fixed in the apartment and the maintenance team worked quickly. Downsides- not a huge fan of the mandatory Valet Trash since I only use it once every few weeks, but they always pick it up, and the Parcel Pending has some issues too. Others are mostly things that aren't the apartment's fault-a decent amount of young renters who don't throw away their trash properly, pick up after their dogs, keep the music down in their cars/apartments, etc. A few homeless people around-again, not the apartment's issue. The area is pretty safe outside a couple porch swipes and car break ins. I've lived in 9 apartments since 2012-a great maintenance and management team makes such a difference. Highly recommended!</Text>

<user_id>104711061737397832516<//user_id><user_name>Timothy Gee</user_name><date>1546919513015< /date><rating>4</rating><text>Former resident here who just recently moved out.  All in all, my wife and I had a great experience living here.  I definitely miss how the apartment is just right by the 76, and how close it is to Sprouts, Petsmart, In 'n' Out, and other restaurants and stores.  The location certainly cannot be beat.

As for the complex itself, it is very clean and well-maintained, with some awesome amenities such as a coffee machine in the office, a 24 hour gym with free weights, and a 24 hour package locker.  Yes, there is a one-time fee for the package locker, but I think it is awesome for the convenience and peace of mind.  And here I am in my current house with a noticeably wider waist, fumbling around with the coffee pot not knowing how much water I need to put in, all while spying constantly out the window for my packages lest the package thief gnomes beat me to them.  Yes, I miss these amenities dearly.

The maintenance staff is probably the best I've ever had out of every apartment complex I've lived at.  Any issue that would come up would be addressed and fixed within 24 hours or less of my request.  The leasing office staff are likewise attentive and courteous.  It helps that they loved my dogs and that my dogs loved them.

The place is not perfect.  There is a mandatory trash service for 20 dollars a month.  This service might be convenient for people who live on the third floor apartments, but we lived not 30 feet away from one of the apartment dumpsters.  We were basically shelling out 20 bucks a month for a service that we never used and couldn't opt out of.  I would ask to see if this policy has changed, as I did notice neighbors who did not seem to have the trash bins for the service.

As other reviews have noted, there definitely can be serious problems with communication, though I suspect the fault lies not with their personnel, but with the means by which they handle communication.  There was a minor incident over our keys when we moved out, with the complex mistakenly believing that we never turned them in when we in fact did.  After two emails and two messages left with their off-site team failed to resolve the issue (we received an additional email from Capella the next day stating that penalties will begin), I had to personally drive to the complex in person.  Turns out the leasing office team never received our messages from the off site team that was supposed to relay them,  or at least the messages simply never showed in their computer system.  Luckily, everything was resolved right then and there, but I can see how frustrating it might be for others trying to contact Capella, especially those who already moved out of state.

Would I live here again?  Absolutely, in a heart beat, despite the flaws. I stayed here for one year. The place is extremely expensive, offers no customer service and has overbearing landlords. When you sign the lease, you agree to pay all the fees to bring the apartment back to "show-room condition" so be prepared to pay $300-500 on top of your security deposit. I showed the lease to a lawyer who said he never seen such a thing in his life, but I signed the lease so lessons learned.

Also, if you are planning on living someplace long term don't come here. They will raise your rent every year. A loophole in California law allows landlords to raise rent every year as long as your notified 90 days in advance of your lease ending, my apartment was set to go up another 150-200 a month (I forget the exact amount).

The apartments look very nice, but the way they are run is extremely shady. This is a business not a home, and unless you are willing to contribute to the business' bottom line, don't become a part of it.< /Review>

<Rating>2< /Rating><Review>I need to place my most recent experience with Skill Craft into context.  I have had repair work done at Skill Craft several times over the past few years.  Each time the work has been expensive, but exceptional.  I keep coming back because I believe that the quality is worth the expense.

So what happened this time???

About three weeks ago I took my 2011 Lexus sedan to Skill Craft to have numerous scratches and scrapes on the hood, doors, fenders and bumpers repaired and refinished.  A Skill Craft estimator INSPECTED the car and we agreed on a price for the repair work.  I left the car and in a few days received a call that the work was complete and that it was ready for pick up.  I picked it up and inspected the work and noticed that the work was of the same outstanding quality I had come to expect from Skill Craft.  I paid the bill and drove home.

A few days later I noticed that the hood had ten or so dimples in the paint.  These were each about 1/8 inch in diameter and shallow in depth.  I could see that the new paint that had been applied by Skill Craft was in the edges and bottom of these dimples, so I knew these dimples were caused by their workers not properly refinishing the hood.  I called Skill Craft and we agreed that I would take it in for their inspection.  I was told there was no hurry to bring the car in because Skill Craft has a lifetime warrantee on their work.  Because of travel out of state I wasn‚Äôt able to take the car to Skill Craft for about two weeks.

When I did take the car back I met with one of their service representatives who told me that the dimples were caused by ‚Äúrock chips‚Äù that were there before the hood was refinished.  I reminded him that he had inspected the hood originally and knew I wanted it to be refinished without ‚Äúrock chips‚Äù showing after finishing.    I asked about the ‚Äúlifetime‚Äù warrantee and I was told the warrantee applies only to the ‚Äúquality‚Äù of their work.

I had to pay several hundred dollars for the cost to refinish the hood again.  I really didn‚Äôt think this was fair nor was it a good business practice‚Ä¶I guess their warrantee of the ‚Äúquality‚Äù of their work doesn‚Äôt apply to the ‚Äúquality‚Äù of their inspection.

<review>Cool little spot near the movie studios to grab breakfast. Lots of gluten free options including pancakes and waffles! They also do a really creative trick/surprise with the foam on their hot drinks.</review><pictures>None</pictures><resp>None< /resp><gmapID>0x80dce801b27f19c1:0xfcfabf636f6bbc9c</gmapID></record>
</dataset><record>
<Resp>None< /Resp><review>For quality made, handy bites for breakfast or lunch in the area, this is a pretty convenient spot. There's easy parking and it's located just across the Irvine train station.They cater to the train commuters ("station") and workers at the nearby business parks with their simple, on-the-go, menu.

I've had a few things here from: breakfast burrito, wraps, panini sandwich, salad and coffee drinks. Breakfast burritos and the chai coffee are solid, paninis are good and filling but isn't greasy and doesn't weigh down heavy. I actually just had their spinach salad with the added tuna salad for my working lunch. This thing is still sitting on my desk, half eaten cause it's quite huge. Nothing fancy but nicely put together and enjoyable. As with anything I've had here, all is made to order.

They have a few tables inside and out. But for the most part, it pretty much is a place for fast, easy and out the door service. They don't deliver but they do take orders over the phone. Pickup is currently the only option. The owners are cool, always friendly and aim to please.

Well, that's about it. Now, back to work.... :)</review>< date>

I have seen my fair share of chiropractors in relation to my SI/hip pain over the past few years, but none have provided me the kind of comprehensive and personal care Dr Benjamin Higier did in just one visit. <rate>4< /rate><name>Kanisha Boer< /name><gmapID>0x80857dc372123eab:0xb09a84cb2ea24603< /gmapID><resp>None< /resp>< Text>
Fancy schmancy ramen at your service! Who would have thought that uni butter miso ramen would actually be a thing AND taste incredibly good?! Because I'm a traditionalist and I'm not really about that gourmet ramen life. I don't need all of that extra hoopla; just gimme the noods with the standard basics and I'm all set. HOWEVER.... I will gladly slurp down a bowl of uniquely flavored ramen from the Ramen Shop any day.

This place is pretty close to where I work, but it took me 3 years to finally give them a try. But why, you ask?! Well let's be honest here; I'm not the type to throw down $20+ on a bowl of ramen. The price tag is steep when compared to other ramen spots. But there's a major difference here when compared to those other spots; the ambience and creativity. The ambience here is like no other. I can totally see why people flock to this place. The vibes are amazing and it's a super fun spot for a date night or even just to chill out with friends.

When you first walk in, you'll be met with the sexy front bar and lounge area. It's dark, it's sultry, it glows at night with their huge alcohol display. Me likey, me likey a lot. But, even more amazing is their actual dining area. It's cozy but effective. They've got beautiful decor and lighting with comfy booths, another back bar, and some counter seating with live cooking action. They play some great music back there too. It's just the ultimate chill spot.

And let me just say, those bartenders really know how to throw down in the bar. The cocktails are delicious and perfectly hand crafted. They tend to change up both their drink and ramen menu quite often, so it allows people to explore so many different kinds of concoctions. Speaking of ramen; the ramen here is quite delicious too. They usually have 3 different ramen flavors on deck that can change as frequently as everyday. Their take on ramen is more explorative than anything else.

I didn't know what to expect since I'm such a traditionalist when it comes to ramen, but I was pleasantly surprised. Ended up having a bowl of their uni butter miso ramen and it damn near blew me away. The culmination of flavors just melded perfectly together. The noodles were a lot softer than I'm used to, but the broth really seeped into them and made them very flavorful.

The bartenders, the host, the owner... EVERYONE was so pleasant to interact with. You can tell that they all really enjoy what they do, and they seem to make an excellent team. Not gonna lie, this place is pretty damn pricey for everyday. But for a nice splurgetastic evening, it's totally worth the money. I will definitely be making a return back.<//Text>

< Review>
Delicious! The ramen menu is simple but the flavors are rich and offer a taste to what you find in Osaka. There's a choice of duck, pork belly or veggie ramen with accompanying garnishes. The noodles are firm and capture the flavors of the broth. They have a well stocked bar with professional mixologists who can conjur anything you could possibly want. I enjoyed the Toki High Ball made with Suntory Toki Whiskey with seltzer and topped with a mint leaf. The coolness of the cocktail paired well with the moderately spicy ramen. If you're a ramen connoisseur, then this is a must visit destination.< /Review>

<time>1475355818886<//time><rate>5<//rate>< Text>
I must say this is a hidden gem between Oakland and Berkeley. Felt a little intimidated at first when I first saw the bowl of Donburi but our server gave us tips on how to truly enjoy this Donburi bowl. Black Cod was cooked to perfection - Buttery and moist and the serving size to me is just right. Embellished with different ingredients, there was a fireworks of flavors in your mouth as soon as I tasted it. The Ramen was so rich and flavorful. The Uni Butter made a huge difference making this miso flavored broth even richer. The pork belly was amazingly tender and the thickness was just right. I like the idea that they change up their menu everyday. Makes me feel like I'm exploring another Ramen place every time.< /Text>

< Review>
9/10 - decor and ambiance
8/10 - service
2/10 - ramen

There's a lot to like about this restaurant, but unfortunately ramen isn't one of them, which is pretty disappointing when their name is "Ramen Shop".  This was some of the worst ramen I've ever had.  The noodles were spongey and I didn't think it was possible to make a broth this bland.  It tasted like hot water.  Completely lacking in umami or salt.

Even if this were half the price this would be very bad ramen.  I would really like to see them drastically improve their broth.  It's a shame that such a nice looking restaurant with such good service has this bad of ramen.

Plus side was that their biscuits were amazing.< /Review>

<name>Coby Ben-Poorat<//name><date>1537420766575<//date>< rating>
5</rating>
< review>
If the Ramen wasn't so expensive (it seems to go up $2 every time I visit) I'd probably eat here weekly. Fantastically cozy atmosphere with tons of wood and low lighting, great service, and rich ramen broth along with a creative drink selection make this one of my local favorites. The full bar/ waiting area is lively and worth getting a drink in if you're waiting for a table, with more upbeat music than the dining area. Some of the other dishes are worth sampling but the Ramen is what brings me back...just be ready to pay $20 for a bowl plus a couple bucks more for chashu, extra egg, or a dumpling add-on. Yum!< /review>

< Review>
Ramen Shop is one of those controversial places, some people either love it or hate it (for the price). I do have to give credit to Ramen Shop for helping kick off the Ramen Renaissance I feel like we now have in the Bay Area. We have so much more ramen than we did ~8 years ago.

As for the ramen itself, I ordered the duck wasabi ramen. The wasabi butter did not have very much wasabi flavor in it, so I was a bit disappointed. If I go back again, I‚Äôd probably order the tonkotsu version, and stick with the classics.<//Review>

<user_name>Jeffrey Alpert< /user_name><date>1511068274288< /date>< rating>
3<//rating>
< review>
Somehow the whole is less than the sum of the parts.  I really can't point out why this ramen just isn't that good.  Technically, the ingredients are good quality, and everything is cooked and seasoned well.  But the soup just isn't that pleasurable to eat.  It seems to be missing its umami flavor - you can taste all the individual ingredients, but there is no savoriness tying it all together.  The beef ramen is over-the-top beefy, like gnawing on a bullion cube, to the point that halfway through the bowl it became slightly unpleasant.  The pork ramen is thick and spicy, but it's missing the savoriness you'd expect of a tonkatsu, so for some reason neither of us really cared to finish that bowl, either.  Excellent noodles, though.  This would simply be a mediocre bowl of ramen if we hadn't waited 90 minutes and paid $20 a bowl.  This was our second attempt at this place, and it hasn't improved at all in the past couple years.  With this hype, and these prices, it's not for us.  It's just not that good.< /review>

<GmapID>0x80857dc372123eab:0xb09a84cb2ea24603< /GmapID>< username>
Phillip Boda<//username>
< review>
Take away from my "miso ramen" dinner: Tomato soup with noodles... But let's itemize. First, EVERY plate, cup, and bowl had multiple chips revealing the ceramic body underneath and it was obvious that the glaze was flaking off - not enjoyable, and sub par in relation to the price point for their food (being a ceramic buff I was just disappointed that they would even give me chopped dinnerware). Second, the waitress we had didn't even ask if we wanted anything to drink, after she took our order she just walked away - I had to stop her and ask for tea; overall bad start to the dinner but I let it slide and hoped the food was worth it (it wasn't). This brings us to 3 - the food - not only was my "miso ramen" more like the consistency of tomato soup, it had minimal "ground pork belly," which was the main protein of the dish. My partner had the beef ramen and let's just say the amount of depth in either broth - you know, the defining characteristic of good ramen - was about as deep as tomato soup. Mine was WAY too thick, lacking flavor, and didn't taste like ramen at all, hence the quotations. My partner's, while thinner, lacked that rich umami flavor I've come to love from any true ramen. Also, don't get the garlic chili paste - it is neither spicy nor is it flavorful. All and all, the only reason this place got 2 stars was because the waitress seemed genuinely interested in replacing my dish when we asked for the check and I said my food was not really that good. $70 later and I would have preferred to just not even try out this restaurant's take on ramen.< /review>

< review>
Any review of this restaurant needs to start with the broth. That dividing liquid line between tasteless mall ramen and those places with quasi-religious followings you find sprinkled throughout Japan and the South Bay. The broth here reaches a depth I had  never known before.  Every time you sip from your spoon, layers of salty, savory, vegetal and earthy tell complicated, inexpressable stories. This broth takes like the end of a quest. The rest of the restaurant lives up to that insane mythical standard too -- the cocktails are simple and perfect (Japanese whiskey abounds), the atmosphere is cozy and hidden (funny because the place is basically in a mini-mall strip of shops on College Avenue), and the servers are friendly and laid-back. Once tasted, never forgotten.</review>

< text>
I had the spicy ramen.  For the premium price ($20/bowl), I was expecting a premium product. It fell waaaay short of the mark they set for themselves.  The flavors were ok, if I was expecting a ramen-bolognese bowl - I wasn't. I didn't find any ground pork belly, but I did find a nice sized garlic skin or something incredibly fibrous in my bowl (after chomping on it hard). I informed the server and received a small apology from her alone.

The service was par/subpar as well.  The simple questions we asked were answered, but often seemed to intially puzzle the server.  Maybe she really didn't know if we could remove one ingredient from a dish.

Decor was nice. Lots of unfinished wood work.  People love that. The light bulbs were very, very cool.  A star for the light bulbs alone.

Again, with the price being so high, the margin for error is razor thin.  Razor thin.  And they chose to serve a bowl of speghetti.  I probably should have just ordered some Japanese whiskey and nothing else.  Maybe next time.< /text>

< text>
This was the best $9 dollar bowl of ramen I've eaten in forever. Pity I paid $16 dollars for it.

The food is creative (the appetizers more-so than the bowls of ramen) but as I dug spoon and chopsticks into my tantamen, I couldn't help feeling a bit scammed. Someone realized the white folks of Rockridge would pay nearly 20 dollars a bowl for Japanese fast-food, complete with ramen noodle, half an egg, a bit of greenery, some creative toppings that are mostly ala carte and broth.

And as I stared around at a room full of ironic glasses, thrift shop aesthetic purchased at top dollar, and people who cared as much about the length of the craft beer selection (longer than the menu) as about the thickness of their wallet, I say "well done" to the owners of Ramen Shop.

This is exactly the who'd pay for it.< /text>

< Text>
Ramen wasnt bad, though the selection was somewhat limited. Broth wasn't too oily but could have used some heat, sadly no spicey options or dried peppers to add to it myself. Flavors where rather basic, nothing too special.

For a beer and basic ramen, ended up being about $35 after tip, for one person. Not really worth it to me to come back, I'll spend the money in gas and goto Santa ramen, ramen dojo, underground ramen or katana-ya.

Drink selection is decent though, may come back to sit at the bar and drink some Japanese whiskey. Though those prices are upped a bit much as well, need to pay for the decore somehow I guess :)

I suggest trying it out, but don't let the hour+ wait make you expect amazing things.< /Text>

103643162894536968927</user>
<response>None<//response><text>Ramen Shop manages to turn ramen into art. Visually, the place is very cool with a bar near the front of the shop. The ramen itself is some of the best the Bay Area has to offer (right up there with Ramen Dojo, Izakaya Sozai, Waraku and Orenchi.)

I went with my friend Al, who's been to Japan times. My favorite all time ramen is still Ippudo in NYC. Totto Ramen is also pretty stellar, but with a lighter broth.

Ramen Shop is very different from all of these places. The focus is on local ingredients you might not even necessarily put in ramen (squash blossoms for example.) The flavors and textures are bold and inspired. It's not meant to be "authentic," just good organic food (since these guys are Alums of Alice Waters resto Chez Panisse.) It succeeds wholeheartedly at that!

We tried a bunch of dishes and drinks. I still think about the Seafood Fried Rice. It's spectacular! The hokkaido miso ramen (ground pork belly, shoyu-marinated egg, corn, pickled carrots, arrowhead cabbage, squash blossom and shungiku) is rich and delicious. The shoyu ramen (chashu, marinated egg, scallions, mizuna, and Mendocino nori) is a little lighter. The pork chashu (porcetta style) is the best I have ever had in a bowl of ramen!

To drink we had the Shop Highball (Hakushu 12-year Japanese Whiskey and soda) and Pimm's Punch (Pimm's, cucumber-infused mezcal, lemon, and ginger beer). I love how they have good Mezcal choices!

Don't skip dessert! The Black Sesame Ice Cream Sandwich is unique and delicious.

Service was attentive and friendly too. Just be prepared for pricing. A bowl of ramen can set you back around $16. I can't wait to go back!</text></record>

<Date>1621697983472< /Date><rate>5< /rate><Text>When we found this place the rating was 4.4, which is good enough but a lot of the good places around here are 4.6 or higher so I was curious why it had a lower rating. When I looked at their prices my eyes popped out a little and so I figured maybe that's why. We had two bowls of ramen, a salad, one sake drink, and dessert for $90. Ramen is ~$20 a bowl + any extras.

However, this place absolutely deserves a higher rating. The ramen was phenomenal. We both had the Shoyu with the garlic chili paste addon. Noodles were perfect and much better than the ones we recently got at Marafuku, the pork was tender and flavorful with properly rendered fat. Excellent marinated egg with a perfect jelly yolk. The broth was simple and delicious. Despite the price we will absolutely be back for more. The outdoor seating is super cute as well. Oh, and get the mochi rice cake dessert.</Text><pictures>None<//pictures><response>None<//response>< gmap_id>
